      <p>
       <b>
        Novosibirsk
       </b>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">
        Russian
       </a>
       :
       <span lang="ru" title="Russian language text">
        Новосиби́рск
       </span>
       ,
       <small>
        IPA:
       </small>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Russian" title="Help:IPA/Russian">
         [nəvəsʲɪˈbʲirsk]
        </a>
       </span>
       ) is the
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_and_towns_in_Russia_by_population" title="List of cities and towns in Russia by population">
        third-most populous
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Types_of_inhabited_localities_in_Russia" title="Types of inhabited localities in Russia">
        city
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">
        Russia
       </a>
       after
       <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">
        Moscow
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">
        St. Petersburg
       </a>
       . It is the most populous city in
       <a href="/wiki/North_Asia" title="North Asia">
        Asian Russia
       </a>
       , with a population of 1,602,900 as of the
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Census_(2010)" title="Russian Census (2010)">
        2010 Census
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2010Census_12-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-2010Census-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Administrative_center" title="Administrative center">
        administrative center
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Novosibirsk_Oblast" title="Novosibirsk Oblast">
        Novosibirsk Oblast
       </a>
       as well as of the
       <a href="/wiki/Siberian_Federal_District" title="Siberian Federal District">
        Siberian Federal District
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The city is located in the southwestern part of
       <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">
        Siberia
       </a>
       on the banks of the
       <a href="/wiki/Ob_River" title="Ob River">
        Ob River
       </a>
       adjacent to the Ob River Valley, near the large
       <a href="/wiki/Novosibirsk_Reservoir" title="Novosibirsk Reservoir">
        water reservoir
       </a>
       formed by the dam of the Novosibirsk Hydro Power Plant.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is split into ten districts and occupies an area of 502.1 square kilometres (193.9 sq mi).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stats_11-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Stats-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Novosibirsk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Novosibirsk" title="Timeline of Novosibirsk">
        Timeline of Novosibirsk
       </a>

          </a>

         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
          Novonikolayevsk in 1895
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px">
         <div class="thumbimage">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Novosibirsk_ANevsky_Cathedral_07-2016_img1.jpg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="3391" data-file-width="3391" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Novosibirsk_ANevsky_Cathedral_07-2016_img1.jpg/200px-Novosibirsk_ANevsky_Cathedral_07-2016_img1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Novosibirsk_ANevsky_Cathedral_07-2016_img1.jpg/300px-Novosibirsk_ANevsky_Cathedral_07-2016_img1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Novosibirsk_ANevsky_Cathedral_07-2016_img1.jpg/400px-Novosibirsk_ANevsky_Cathedral_07-2016_img1.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
          <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Nevsky_Cathedral,_Novosibirsk" title="Alexander Nevsky Cathedral, Novosibirsk">
           St. Alexander Nevsky Cathedral
          </a>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Novosibirsk, founded in 1893
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Established_16-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Established-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       at the future site of a
       <a href="/wiki/Trans-Siberian_Railway" title="Trans-Siberian Railway">
        Trans-Siberian Railway
       </a>
       bridge crossing the great Siberian river of
       <a href="/wiki/Ob_River" title="Ob River">
        Ob
       </a>
       , first was named
       <b>
        Novonikolayevsk
       </b>
       (
       <span lang="ru" title="Russian language text">
        Новониколаевск
       </span>
       ),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Names_17-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Names-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       in honor both of
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Nicholas" title="Saint Nicholas">
        Saint Nicholas
       </a>
       and of the reigning
       <a href="/wiki/Tsar" title="Tsar">
        Tsar
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_II_of_Russia" title="Nicholas II of Russia">
        Nicholas II
       </a>
       . It superseded nearby Krivoshchekovskaya village, which was founded in 1696. The bridge was completed in the spring of 1897, making the new settlement the regional transport hub. The importance of the city further increased with the completion of the
       <a href="/wiki/Turkestan%E2%80%93Siberia_Railway" title="Turkestan–Siberia Railway">
        Turkestan-Siberia Railway
       </a>
       in the early 20th century. The new railway connected Novonikolayevsk to
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">
        Central Asia
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Sea" title="Caspian Sea">
        Caspian Sea
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-all_21-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-all-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       At the time of the bridge's opening, Novonikolayevsk had a population of 7,800 people. The frontier settlement developed rapidly. Its first bank opened in 1906, and a total of five banks were operating by 1915. In 1907, Novonikolayevsk, now with a population exceeding 47,000, was granted town status with full rights for self-government. During the pre-
       <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution">
        revolutionary
       </a>
       period, the population of Novonikolayevsk reached 80,000. The city had steady and rapid
       <a href="/wiki/Economic_growth" title="Economic growth">
        economic growth
       </a>
       , becoming one of the largest commercial and industrial centers of
       <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">
        Siberia
       </a>
       . It developed a significant agricultural processing industry,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       as well as a
       <a href="/wiki/Power_station" title="Power station">
        power station
       </a>
       , iron foundry, commodity market, several banks, and commercial and shipping companies. By 1917, seven Orthodox churches and one
       <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">
        Roman Catholic
       </a>
       church had been built there, several cinemas, forty
       <a href="/wiki/Primary_education" title="Primary education">
        primary schools
       </a>
       , a high school, a teaching seminary, and the Romanov House non-classical
       <a href="/wiki/Secondary_school" title="Secondary school">
        secondary school
       </a>
       . In 1913, Novonikolayevsk became one of the first places in Russia to institute compulsory primary education.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-all_21-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-all-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Civil_War" title="Russian Civil War">
        Russian Civil War
       </a>
       took a toll on the city. There were wartime epidemics, especially of
       <a href="/wiki/Typhus" title="Typhus">
        typhus
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Cholera" title="Cholera">
        cholera
       </a>
       , that claimed thousands of lives. In the course of the war the Ob River Bridge was destroyed. For the first time in the city's history, the population of Novonikolayevsk began to decline. The Soviet Workers' and Soldiers' Deputies of Novonikolayevsk took control of the city in December 1917. In May 1918, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Czechoslovak_Legions" title="Czechoslovak Legions">
        Czechoslovak Legions
       </a>
       rose in opposition to the revolutionary government and, together with the
       <a href="/wiki/White_movement" title="White movement">
        White Guards
       </a>
       , captured Novonikolayevsk. The
       <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">
        Red Army
       </a>
       took the city in 1919, retaining it throughout the rest of the Civil War.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-all_21-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-all-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Novonikolayevsk began reconstruction in 1921 at the start of
       <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">
        Lenin
       </a>
       's
       <a href="/wiki/New_Economic_Policy" title="New Economic Policy">
        New Economic Policy
       </a>
       period. It was a part of
       <a href="/wiki/Tomsk_Governorate" title="Tomsk Governorate">
        Tomsk Governorate
       </a>
       and served as its administrative center from December 23, 1919 to March 14, 1920.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Between June 13, 1921 and May 25, 1925, it served as the administrative center of
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Novonikolayevsk_Governorate&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Novonikolayevsk Governorate (page does not exist)">
        Novonikolayevsk Governorate
       </a>
       , which was separated from Tomsk Governorate.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       The city was given its present name on September 12, 1926.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Names_17-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-Names-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       When governorates were abolished, the city served as the administrative center of
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Siberian_Krai&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Siberian Krai (page does not exist)">
        Siberian Krai
       </a>
       until July 23, 1930, and of
       <a href="/wiki/West_Siberian_Krai" title="West Siberian Krai">
        West Siberian Krai
       </a>
       until September 28, 1937, when that krai was split into
       <a href="/wiki/Novosibirsk_Oblast" title="Novosibirsk Oblast">
        Novosibirsk Oblast
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Altai_Krai" title="Altai Krai">
        Altai Krai
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-base.consultant.ru_23-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-base.consultant.ru-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Since then, it has served as the administrative center of Novosibirsk Oblast.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-base.consultant.ru_23-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-base.consultant.ru-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Monument_to_the_Heroes_of_the_Revolution" title="Monument to the Heroes of the Revolution">
        Monument to the Heroes of the Revolution
       </a>
       was erected in the center of the city and has been one of the chief historic sites (essentially every child had to visit the monument on school field trips during the Soviet years). Neglect in the 1990s while other areas were redeveloped helped preserve it in the post-Soviet era.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       During
       <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">
        Joseph Stalin
       </a>
       's industrialization effort, Novosibirsk secured its place as one of the largest industrial centers of Siberia. Several massive industrial facilities were created, including the 'Sibkombain' plant, specializing in the production of heavy mining equipment. Additionally a metal processing plant, a food processing plant and other industrial enterprises and factories were built, as well as a new
       <a href="/wiki/Power_station" title="Power station">
        power station
       </a>
       . The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet_famine_of_1932%E2%80%931933" title="Soviet famine of 1932–1933">
        Great Soviet Famine
       </a>
       of 1932-1933 resulted in more than 170,000 rural refugees seeking food and safety in Novosibirsk. They were settled in barracks at the outskirts of the city, giving rise to slums such as Bolshaya Nakhalovka, Malaya Nakhalovka, and others.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-all_21-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-all-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Its rapid growth and industrialization led to Novosibirsk being nicknamed the "
       <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">
        Chicago
       </a>
       of Siberia".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Tram rails were laid down in 1934, by which time the population had reached 287,000, making Novosibirsk the largest city in Siberia. The following year the original bridge over the Ob River was replaced by the new Kommunalny bridge.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-all_21-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-all-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Between 1940 and 1942 more than 50 substantial factories were crated up and relocated from western Russia to Novosibirsk in order to reduce the risk of their destruction through
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Patriotic_War" title="Great Patriotic War">
        war
       </a>
       , and at this time the city became a major supply base for the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_army" title="Red army">
        Red army
       </a>
       . During this period the city also received more than 140,000 refugees.
      </p>
      <p>
       The rapid growth of the city prompted the construction during the 1950s of a
       <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectricity" title="Hydroelectricity">
        hydroelectric power station
       </a>
       with a capacity of 400
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Megawatt" title="Megawatt">
        megawatts
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       necessitating the creation of a giant water reservoir, now known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Novosibirsk_Reservoir" title="Novosibirsk Reservoir">
        Ob Sea
       </a>
       . As a direct result of the station's construction vast areas of fertile land were flooded as were relic pine woods in the area; additionally, the new open space created by the reservoir's surface caused average wind speeds to double, increasing the rate of
       <a href="/wiki/Erosion" title="Erosion">
        soil erosion
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-all_21-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-all-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the 1950s, the Soviet Government directed that a center for scientific research be built in Novosibirsk, and in 1957 the multi-facility
       <a href="/wiki/Science" title="Science">
        scientific
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Research" title="Research">
        research
       </a>
       complex of
       <a href="/wiki/Akademgorodok" title="Akademgorodok">
        Akademgorodok
       </a>
       was constructed about 30 kilometers (19 mi) south of the city center. The Siberian Division of the Academy of Sciences has its headquarters in
       <a href="/wiki/Akademgorodok" title="Akademgorodok">
        Akademgorodok
       </a>
       , and the town hosts more than 35 research institutes and universities, among them
       <a href="/wiki/Novosibirsk_State_University" title="Novosibirsk State University">
        Novosibirsk State University
       </a>
       , one of the top Russian schools in Natural Sciences and Mathematics. Although it possesses a fully autonomous infrastructure, Akademgorodok is administered by Novosibirsk.
      </p>
      <p>
       On September 2, 1962, the population of Novosibirsk reached one million. At that time, it was the youngest city in the world with over a million people. Novosibirsk took fewer than seventy years to achieve this milestone.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1979, work began on the
       <a href="/wiki/Novosibirsk_Metro" title="Novosibirsk Metro">
        Novosibirsk Metro Transit System
       </a>
       , culminating in the opening of the first line in 1985.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-all_21-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-all-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On August 1, 2008, Novosibirsk was in the center of the path of a
       <a href="/wiki/Solar_eclipse_of_August_1,_2008" title="Solar eclipse of August 1, 2008">
        solar eclipse
       </a>
       , with a duration of 2 minutes and 20 seconds.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_and_municipal_status">
        Administrative and municipal status
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Novosibirsk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Administrative and municipal status">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%90%D0%B4%D0%BC%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%9D%D0%A1%D0%9E.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="476" data-file-width="750" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/%D0%90%D0%B4%D0%BC%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%9D%D0%A1%D0%9E.jpg/220px-%D0%90%D0%B4%D0%BC%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%9D%D0%A1%D0%9E.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/%D0%90%D0%B4%D0%BC%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%9D%D0%A1%D0%9E.jpg/330px-%D0%90%D0%B4%D0%BC%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%9D%D0%A1%D0%9E.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/%D0%90%D0%B4%D0%BC%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%9D%D0%A1%D0%9E.jpg/440px-%D0%90%D0%B4%D0%BC%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%9D%D0%A1%D0%9E.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%90%D0%B4%D0%BC%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%82%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%9D%D0%A1%D0%9E.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The administrative building of
         <a href="/wiki/Novosibirsk_Oblast" title="Novosibirsk Oblast">
          Novosibirsk Oblast
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Novosibirsk is the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Administrative_center" title="Administrative center">
        administrative center
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Oblast" title="Oblast">
        oblast
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OblastAdmCtr_4-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-OblastAdmCtr-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and, within the
       <a href="/wiki/Subdivisions_of_Russia#Administrative_divisions" title="Subdivisions of Russia">
        framework of administrative divisions
       </a>
       , it also serves as the administrative center of
       <a href="/wiki/Novosibirsky_District" title="Novosibirsky District">
        Novosibirsky District
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OKATO1_1-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-OKATO1-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       even though it is not a part of it.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OKATO2_5-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-OKATO2-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As an administrative division, it is incorporated separately as the
       <b>
        <a href="/wiki/City_of_federal_subject_significance" title="City of federal subject significance">
         City
        </a>
        of Novosibirsk
       </b>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OKATO2_5-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-OKATO2-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       —an administrative unit with the status equal to that of the
       <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Novosibirsk_Oblast" title="Administrative divisions of Novosibirsk Oblast">
        districts
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2012)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       As a
       <a href="/wiki/Subdivisions_of_Russia#Municipal_divisions" title="Subdivisions of Russia">
        municipal division
       </a>
       , the City of Novosibirsk is incorporated as
       <b>
        Novosibirsk Urban Okrug
       </b>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NovosibirskO_mun_6-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-NovosibirskO_mun-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">
        Demographics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Novosibirsk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Demographics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table class="infobox" style="width:22em">
       <caption>
        Novosibirsk population
       </caption>

         </a>
        </th>

         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2010Census_12-2">

         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>

         </a>
        </th>

         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2002Census_27-0">

        </td>
       </tr>

         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1989Census_28-0">

       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       According to the
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Federal_State_Statistics_Service" title="Russian Federal State Statistics Service">
        Federal State Statistics Service
       </a>
       , in January 2015 the number of residents came to 1,567,087.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2015Est_13-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-2015Est-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This is an increase compared to the
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Census_(2010)" title="Russian Census (2010)">
        2010 Census
       </a>
       , when the population of the city was 1,473,754.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2010Census_12-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-2010Census-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       People from over eighty ethnicities and nationalities reside in Novosibirsk. The largest groups are
       <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">
        Russian
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Yakuts" title="Yakuts">
        Yakut
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Germans_in_Russia" title="Germans in Russia">
        German
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians_in_Russia" title="Ukrainians in Russia">
        Ukrainian
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tatars" title="Tatars">
        Tatar
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jews_in_Russia" title="Jews in Russia">
        Jewish
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Belarusians" title="Belarusians">
        Belarusian
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ecology">
        Ecology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Novosibirsk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Ecology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Flora">
        Flora
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Novosibirsk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Flora">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The best-known trees native to Novosibirsk are
       <a href="/wiki/Birch" title="Birch">
        birch
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Pine" title="Pine">
        pine
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Aspen" title="Aspen">
        aspen
       </a>
       . Some
       <a href="/wiki/Sorbus_aucuparia" title="Sorbus aucuparia">
        mountain ash
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Crataegus_monogyna" title="Crataegus monogyna">
        hawthorn
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Spruce" title="Spruce">
        spruce
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Fir" title="Fir">
        fir
       </a>
       are also present. European species of
       <a href="/wiki/Apple" title="Apple">
        apple
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Fraxinus" title="Fraxinus">
        ash
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Elm" title="Elm">
        elm
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tilia" title="Tilia">
        linden
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Oak" title="Oak">
        oak
       </a>
       have been successfully introduced.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">
        Geography
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Novosibirsk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Geography">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Location">
        Location
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Novosibirsk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Location">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The city stands on the banks of the Ob River in the
       <a href="/wiki/West_Siberian_Plain" title="West Siberian Plain">
        West Siberian Plain
       </a>
       . To the south of the city lies The Priobskoye Plateau.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%91%D1%83%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BC%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82_%D0%9D%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%B1%D0%B8%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA_II.PNG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="514" data-file-width="979" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/%D0%91%D1%83%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BC%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82_%D0%9D%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%B1%D0%B8%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA_II.PNG/300px-%D0%91%D1%83%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BC%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82_%D0%9D%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%B1%D0%B8%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA_II.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/%D0%91%D1%83%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BC%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82_%D0%9D%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%B1%D0%B8%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA_II.PNG/450px-%D0%91%D1%83%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BC%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82_%D0%9D%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%B1%D0%B8%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA_II.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/%D0%91%D1%83%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BC%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82_%D0%9D%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%B1%D0%B8%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA_II.PNG/600px-%D0%91%D1%83%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BC%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82_%D0%9D%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%B1%D0%B8%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA_II.PNG 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%91%D1%83%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%BC%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%82_%D0%9D%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%B1%D0%B8%D1%80%D1%81%D0%BA_II.PNG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Bugrinsky_Bridge" title="Bugrinsky Bridge">
          Bugrinsky Bridge
         </a>
         on the
         <a href="/wiki/Ob_River" title="Ob River">
          Ob River
         </a>
        </div>

      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">
        Climate
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Novosibirsk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Climate">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The weather in Novosibirsk is like the rest of typical Siberia, with a clear sky and far below freezing winter temperatures. The reason for these temperatures is the absence of nearby ocean, the
       <a href="/wiki/Ural_Mountains" title="Ural Mountains">
        Ural Mountains
       </a>
       , barring Atlantic air masses from reaching Siberia, and the lack of tall mountains at the north of Novosibirsk, that could have held back freezing Arctic winds. In fact, Novosibirsk is the second farthest substantially populated city from the ocean, the first being
       <a href="/wiki/%C3%9Cr%C3%BCmqi" title="Ürümqi">
        Ürümqi
       </a>
       in China.
      </p>
      <p>
       The climate is
       <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">
        humid continental
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">
        Köppen
       </a>
       <i>
        Dfb
       </i>
       ), with warm summers and bitterly cold winters. Snow is frequent, falling on almost half of all winter days, but individual snowfalls are usually light. On average temperatures range in summer from +15 °C (59 °F) to +26 °C (79 °F) and in winter from −20 °C (−4 °F) to −12 °C (10 °F). However, winter temperatures can go as low as −30 °C (−22 °F) to −35 °C (−31 °F), and summer temperatures can go as high as +30 °C (86 °F) to +35 °C (95 °F). The difference between the highest and lowest recorded temperatures is 88 °C (158 °F).
      </p>
      <p>
       Travellers coming from countries with mild climates may find Novosibirsk’s winter tough, but it may not be extraordinary for those from northern countries. At times, bitter cold may hold for some days, but temperatures of −40 °C (−40 °F) and lower do not occur every year. In the springtime, streets and roads become dirty as a result of mud and melting snow, while the weather is still cold.
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Broadcasting">
        Broadcasting
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Novosibirsk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Broadcasting">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Novosibirsk is home to Russia's most powerful
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shortwave" title="Shortwave">
        shortwave
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Microwave_radio_relay" title="Microwave radio relay">
        relay station
       </a>
       east of the
       <a href="/wiki/Ural_Mountains" title="Ural Mountains">
        Ural mountains
       </a>
       . This relay station can reach most of
       <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">
        South Asia
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">
        Middle East
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="People's Republic of China">
        China
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Magadan" title="Magadan">
        Magadan
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Vladivostok" title="Vladivostok">
        Vladivostok
       </a>
       relay stations when operated in conjunction with Novosibirsk can guarantee that the
       <a href="/wiki/Voice_of_Russia" title="Voice of Russia">
        Voice of Russia
       </a>
       or any other broadcaster renting time at Novosibirsk is heard in the intended target area.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">
        Transportation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Novosibirsk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Transportation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:368px;max-width:368px">
        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px">
         <div class="thumbimage">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Novosibirsk_Glavny_Station_07-2016_img3.jpg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="2667" data-file-width="4268" height="112" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Novosibirsk_Glavny_Station_07-2016_img3.jpg/180px-Novosibirsk_Glavny_Station_07-2016_img3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Novosibirsk_Glavny_Station_07-2016_img3.jpg/270px-Novosibirsk_Glavny_Station_07-2016_img3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Novosibirsk_Glavny_Station_07-2016_img3.jpg/360px-Novosibirsk_Glavny_Station_07-2016_img3.jpg 2x" width="180"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">
          Novosibirsk Trans-Siberian railway station
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:182px;max-width:182px">
         <div class="thumbimage">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nsk-Ob_Tolmachevo_terminal_07-2016.jpg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="3171" data-file-width="5073" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Nsk-Ob_Tolmachevo_terminal_07-2016.jpg/180px-Nsk-Ob_Tolmachevo_terminal_07-2016.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Nsk-Ob_Tolmachevo_terminal_07-2016.jpg/270px-Nsk-Ob_Tolmachevo_terminal_07-2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Nsk-Ob_Tolmachevo_terminal_07-2016.jpg/360px-Nsk-Ob_Tolmachevo_terminal_07-2016.jpg 2x" width="180"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">
          Tolmachevo Airport
         </div>
        </div>
        <div style="clear:left">
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Novosibirsk is the third-largest city in Russia (after Moscow and St. Petersburg) and the first in Siberia in which a
       <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">
        metro
       </a>
       system was established (the
       <a href="/wiki/Novosibirsk_Metro" title="Novosibirsk Metro">
        Novosibirsk Metro
       </a>
       , opened in 1985). It is a major stop on the
       <a href="/wiki/Trans-Siberian_Railway" title="Trans-Siberian Railway">
        Trans-Siberian Railway
       </a>
       and north end of
       <a href="/wiki/Turkestan%E2%80%93Siberia_Railway" title="Turkestan–Siberia Railway">
        Turkestan–Siberia Railway
       </a>
       . The city is served by
       <a href="/wiki/Tolmachevo_Airport" title="Tolmachevo Airport">
        Novosibirsk Tolmachevo Airport
       </a>
       with regular flights to Europe and Asia as well as to other Russian cities. Tolmachevo is the hub for
       <a href="/wiki/S7_Airlines" title="S7 Airlines">
        S7 Airlines
       </a>
       . There is also the auxiliary
       <a href="/wiki/Yeltsovka_Airport" title="Yeltsovka Airport">
        Yeltsovka Airport
       </a>
       . A smaller field for
       <a href="/wiki/General_aviation" title="General aviation">
        general aviation
       </a>
       at
       <a href="/wiki/Severny_Airport" title="Severny Airport">
        Novosibirsk Severny Airport
       </a>
       was closed in 2012.
      </p>
      <p>
       From other modes of transport there is a bus (launched in 1923), tram (launched in 1934), trolleybus (launched in 1957) and
       <a href="/wiki/Marshrutka" title="Marshrutka">
        marshrutkas
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">

           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallerytext">
          <p>
           Marshal Pokryshkin metro station
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Novosibirsk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Economy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Novosibirsk_Kommunisticheskaya_50.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="960" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Novosibirsk_Kommunisticheskaya_50.jpg/170px-Novosibirsk_Kommunisticheskaya_50.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Novosibirsk_Kommunisticheskaya_50.jpg/255px-Novosibirsk_Kommunisticheskaya_50.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Novosibirsk_Kommunisticheskaya_50.jpg/340px-Novosibirsk_Kommunisticheskaya_50.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Novosibirsk_Kommunisticheskaya_50.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         One of the city's new high-rises, photo from 2006
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Novosibirsk is a large industrial center. The industrial complex consists of 214 large and average sized industrial enterprises. These produce more than two-thirds of all industrial output of the Novosibirsk region. Leading industries are airspace (Chkalov's Novosibirsk Aircraft Plant), nuclear fuel (Novosibirsk Chemical Concentrates Plant), turbo- and hydroelectric generators (NPO ELSIB), textile machinery (Textilmach), agriculture machinery (NPO "Sibselmash"), electronics components and devices production (Novosibirsk Factory and Design Bureau of Semiconductor Devices NZPP, OXID Novosibirsk Plant of Radio components), metallurgy and metal working (Kuzmina's Novosibirsk Metallurgical Plant, Novosibirsk Tin Plant" OJSC, and JSC "Plant of Rare Metals).
      </p>
      <p>
       According to the television station RBC Novosibirsk took third place in 2008 in the list of the cities of Russia most attractive to business (in 2007 it was placed thirteenth).
      </p>
      <p>
       Before the relocation of its headquarters to
       <a href="/wiki/Ob,_Russia" title="Ob, Russia">
        Ob
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/S7_Airlines" title="S7 Airlines">
        S7 Airlines
       </a>
       had its head office in Novosibirsk.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Headquarters" title="Headquarters">
        headquarters
       </a>
       of a number of large Russian companies are located in Novosibirsk:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        RATM Holding
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Antonov" title="Antonov">
         Antonov
        </a>
        (Aircraft company) NAPO named after Chkalov
       </li>
       <li>
        Belon
       </li>
       <li>
        The Siberian coast» Food Company (until 2009)
       </li>
       <li>
        NETA IT Company (retail, system integrator, software sales)
       </li>
       <li>
        Parallels IT Company (software for virtualization)
       </li>
       <li>
        Inmarko Food Company
       </li>
       <li>
        Siberian Food Corporation
       </li>
       <li>
        Electro-vacuum plant (the largest glass bottles factory in Asian part of country)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/NIIIP" title="NIIIP">
         NPO NIIIP-NZiK
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/2GIS" title="2GIS">
         2GIS
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>

      <p>
       Novosibirsk is the home town of several former Olympians, including
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alexander_Karelin" title="Alexander Karelin">
        Alexander Karelin
       </a>
       , a twelve-time world
       <a href="/wiki/Greco-Roman_wrestling" title="Greco-Roman wrestling">
        Greco-Roman wrestling
       </a>
       champion who has been voted the greatest Greco-Roman wrestler of the twentieth century by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Federation_of_Associated_Wrestling_Styles" title="International Federation of Associated Wrestling Styles">
        FILA
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The city also hosts a number of National and International
       <a href="/wiki/Ice_speedway" title="Ice speedway">
        Ice Speedway
       </a>
       events. Siberia Novosibirsk competed in the Russian Ice Speedway Premier League in 2012/13, and will do so again in 2013/2014.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Music">
        Music
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Novosibirsk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Music">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Several contemporary classical violinists, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Vadim_Repin" title="Vadim Repin">
        Vadim Repin
       </a>
       , the late Alexander Skwortsow,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Natalia_Lomeiko&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Natalia Lomeiko (page does not exist)">
        Natalia Lomeiko
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Maxim_Vengerov" title="Maxim Vengerov">
        Maxim Vengerov
       </a>
       , are natives of Novosibirsk. Also born in the city were punk legend, poet and singer-songwriter
       <a href="/wiki/Yanka_Dyagileva" title="Yanka Dyagileva">
        Yanka Dyagileva
       </a>
       , tragic punk rocker
       <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Selivanov" title="Dmitry Selivanov">
        Dmitry Selivanov
       </a>
       , folk/folk–rock singer Pelageya Khanova and cellist
       <a href="/wiki/Tatjana_Vassiljeva" title="Tatjana Vassiljeva">
        Tatjana Vassiljeva
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The city possesses a Conservatory (named in honor of
       <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Glinka" title="Mikhail Glinka">
        Mikhail Glinka
       </a>
       ); Novosibirsk State Philharmony, that is home for Novosibirsk Academic Symphony Orchestra, Novosibirsk Philharmonic Chamber Orchestra, Russian Academic Orchestra of Folk Instruments, and other musical groups;
       <a href="/wiki/Novosibirsk_Opera_and_Ballet_Theatre" title="Novosibirsk Opera and Ballet Theatre">
        Novosibirsk Opera and Ballet Theater
       </a>
       , and several notable music venues.
      </p>

      </h2>

         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Akademgorodok_Airphoto.jpg/220px-Akademgorodok_Airphoto.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Akademgorodok_Airphoto.jpg/330px-Akademgorodok_Airphoto.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Akademgorodok_Airphoto.jpg/440px-Akademgorodok_Airphoto.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Akademgorodok_Airphoto.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Airphoto of
         <a href="/wiki/Akademgorodok" title="Akademgorodok">
          Akademgorodok
         </a>
        </div>

      </div>
      <p>
       Novosibirsk is home to the following high educational institutions (masters level degree and PhD):
      </p>
      <div class="div-col columns column-count column-count-2" style="-moz-column-count: 2; -webkit-column-count: 2; column-count: 2;">
       <ul>
        <li>

         </a>

        </li>

         </a>
        </li>
        <li>
         <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Novosibirsk_State_Architecture_and_Construction_University&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Novosibirsk State Architecture and Construction University (page does not exist)">

         </a>

        </li>

        </li>

      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Akademgorodok" title="Akademgorodok">
        Akademgorodok
       </a>
       is a suburb of Novosibirsk dedicated to science. It houses the Siberian division of the Russian Academy of Sciences and is the location of Novosibirsk State University. (All other higher education institutions are located in the central part of the city.)
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Quality_Schools_International" title="Quality Schools International">
        Quality Schools International
       </a>
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=QSI_International_School_of_Novosibirsk&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="QSI International School of Novosibirsk (page does not exist)">
        QSI International School of Novosibirsk
       </a>
       , previously located in Akademgorodok, opened in 2008.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Novosibirsk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Cinemas">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       16 cinemas, including Cinema Park which supports
       <a href="/wiki/IMAX" title="IMAX">
        IMAX
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IMAX_3D" title="IMAX 3D">
        IMAX 3D
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">
        Museums
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

        </span>
       </span>

       </li>

       </li>

        </a>
        glory
       </li>
       <li>
        Novosibirsk museum of railway equipment named after N.A. Akulinin
       </li>

        <a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Roerich" title="Nicholas Roerich">

        </a>

       </li>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Planetarium">
        Planetarium
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Novosibirsk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Planetarium">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Novosibirsk_Planetarium&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Novosibirsk Planetarium (page does not exist)">
        Novosibirsk Planetarium
       </a>
       (2012)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       was awarded in 2015 as the best social infrastructure object in Russia.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

        </span>

        Central Siberian Botanical Garden

          [41]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Novosibirsk_Zoo">
        Novosibirsk Zoo
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Novosibirsk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Novosibirsk Zoo">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Novosibirsk_Zoo" title="Novosibirsk Zoo">
        Novosibirsk Zoo
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Novosibirsk_Zoo" title="Novosibirsk Zoo">
        Novosibirsk Zoo
       </a>
       is a world-renowned scientific institution as well as a popular
       <a href="/wiki/Tourist_attraction" title="Tourist attraction">
        tourist attraction
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Zoo" title="Zoo">
        zoo
       </a>
       has over 11000 animals from 738 species and is an active participant in thirty-two different
       <a href="/wiki/Captive_breeding" title="Captive breeding">
        captive breeding
       </a>
       programmes for endangered species. On average, around 1,5 million people visit the zoo each year.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns_and_sister_cities">
        Twin towns and sister cities
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_residents">
        Notable residents
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Novosibirsk&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Notable residents">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Novosibirsk" title="List of people from Novosibirsk">
        List of people from Novosibirsk
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Violinist
       <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Simonyan" title="Mikhail Simonyan">
        Mikhail Simonyan
       </a>
       , playwright and prose writer
       <a href="/wiki/Nina_Mikhailovna_Sadur" title="Nina Mikhailovna Sadur">
        Nina Mikhailovna Sadur
       </a>
       , and three-time Olympic Greco-Roman wrestling champion
       <a href="/wiki/Aleksandr_Karelin" title="Aleksandr Karelin">
        Aleksandr Karelin
       </a>
       were born and raised in Novosibirsk.
      </p>

       <li>
        <span lang="ru" title="Russian language text">
         Городской Совет Новосибирска. Решение №616 от 27 июня 2007 г. «Устав города Новосибирска», в ред. Решения №1311 от 31 марта 2015 г. «О внесении изменений в устав города Новосибирска, принятый Решением городского Совета Новосибирска от 27.06.2007 №616». Вступил в силу через 10 дней со дня официального опубликования, за исключением положений, для которых установлены иные сроки и порядок вступления в силу. Опубликован: "Бюллетень органов городского самоуправления Новосибирска", №58, стр. 3, 15 августа 2007 г.
        </span>
        (City Council of Novosibirsk. Decision #616 of June 27, 2007
        <i>
         Charter of the City of Novosibirsk
        </i>
        , as amended by the Decision #1311 of March 31, 2015
        <i>
         On Amending the Charter of the City of Novosibirsk Adopted by the Decision #616 of the City Council of Novosibirsk of June 27, 2007
        </i>
        . Effective as of 10 days after the official publication date, with the exception of the clauses for which different dates and procedures of taking effect are specified.).
       </li>
       <li>
        <span lang="ru" title="Russian language text">
         Новосибирский областной Совет депутатов. Постановление №282-ОЗ от 31 марта 2005 г. «
         <a class="external text" href="http://zsnso.ru/116/#_Toc266437147" rel="nofollow">
          Устав Новосибирской области
         </a>
         », в ред. Закона №529-ОЗ от 26 февраля 2015 г. «О поправках к Уставу Новосибирской области». Вступил в силу 1 мая 2005 г. Опубликован: "Советская Сибирь", №81, 29 апреля 2005 г.
        </span>
        (Novosibirsk Oblast Council of Deputies. Resolution #282-OZ of March 31, 2005
        <i>
         <a class="external text" href="http://translate.google.com/translate?hl=en&amp;sl=ru&amp;tl=en&amp;u=http://zsnso.ru/116/#_Toc266437147" rel="nofollow">
          Charter of Novosibirsk Oblast

        </i>
        , as amended by the Law #529-OZ of February 26, 2015

        </i>
        . Effective as of May 1, 2005.).
       </li>
       <li>
        <span lang="ru" title="Russian language text">
         Новосибирский областной Совет депутатов. Закон №246-ОЗ от 17 декабря 2004 г. «Об административных центрах муниципальных районов и сельских поселений Новосибирской области», в ред. Закона №69-ОЗ от 5 декабря 2006 г. «О внесении изменений в Закон Новосибирской области "Об административных центрах муниципальных районов и сельских поселений Новосибирской области"». Вступил в силу со дня официального опубликования. Опубликован: "Советская Сибирь", №252, 29 декабря 2004 г.
        </span>
        (Novosibirsk Oblast Council of Deputies. Law #246-OZ of December 17, 2004
        <i>
         On the Administrative Centers of the Municipal Districts and Rural Settlements of Novosibirsk Oblast
        </i>
        , as amended by the Law #69-OZ of December 5, 2006
        <i>
         On Amending the Law of Novosibirsk Oblast "On the Administrative Centers of the Municipal Districts and Rural Settlements of Novosibirsk Oblast"
        </i>
        . Effective as of the official publication date.).
       </li>
